         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="417" data-file-width="640" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Walter_Kitundu.jpg/300px-Walter_Kitundu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Walter_Kitundu.jpg/450px-Walter_Kitundu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Walter_Kitundu.jpg/600px-Walter_Kitundu.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Walter_Kitundu.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Walter_Kitundu" title="Walter Kitundu">
          Walter Kitundu
         </a>
         - Artist in Residence and MacArthur Fellow
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Despite being generally thought of as a science museum, the Exploratorium has always incorporated both science and art. As early as 1966, Frank Oppenheimer presented a paper discussing the connections between art and science, and the role of a museum in appealing to both casual visitors and serious students of all ages.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cole_9-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-Cole-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         142
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The formal artist in residence program was started in 1974,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AIR_75-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AIR-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but artworks such as Bob Miller’s
       <i>
        Sun Painting
       </i>
       were commissioned shortly after the museum was opened in 1969.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BobMiller_76-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BobMiller-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since the founding of the artist in residence program, over 250 artworks in various disciplines have been created.
      </p>
      <p>
       Each year, the museum invites ten to twenty artists to participate in residencies ranging from two weeks to two years. Artists-in-residence work with staff and the visiting public to create original installations, exhibits, or performances. Artists are given a stipend, housing, travel expenses, and technical support, and they have at their disposal the Exploratorium's full array of metal and woodworking shops and materials. Two artists-in-residence who went on to become staff members have been awarded
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MacArthur_Fellowship" title="MacArthur Fellowship">
        MacArthur Fellowship
       </a>
       "genius" grants:
       <a href="/wiki/Walter_Kitundu" title="Walter Kitundu">
        Walter Kitundu
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ned_Kahn" title="Ned Kahn">
        Ned Kahn
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The new Embarcadero campus opened with more than 40 pieces by prominent artists, including Douglas Hollis,
       <a href="/wiki/Golan_Levin" title="Golan Levin">
        Golan Levin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lucky_Dragons" title="Lucky Dragons">
        Lucky Dragons
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Amy_Balkin" title="Amy Balkin">
        Amy Balkin
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Fujiko_Nakaya" title="Fujiko Nakaya">
        Fujiko Nakaya
       </a>
       . The Center for Art and Inquiry, a new project at the new location, is an initiative to catalyze and orchestrate art across the museum.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miranda_53-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Miranda-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Exploratorium has an equally long history with musical, film and other performances. Participating artists and performers included
       <a href="/wiki/Laurie_Anderson" title="Laurie Anderson">
        Laurie Anderson
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/John_Cage" title="John Cage">
        John Cage
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Philip_Glass" title="Philip Glass">
        Philip Glass
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Steve_Reich" title="Steve Reich">
        Steve Reich
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Brian_Eno" title="Brian Eno">
        Brian Eno
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ali_Akbar_Khan" title="Ali Akbar Khan">
        Ali Akbar Khan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Trimpin" title="Trimpin">
        Trimpin
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/The_Mermen" title="The Mermen">
        The Mermen
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Speakingofmusic_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Speakingofmusic-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition to the artists in residence, the museum’s Osher Fellows Program hosts 4-8 resident scholars, scientists, educators, and artists every year. Notable Osher Fellows have included
       <a href="/wiki/Walter_Murch" title="Walter Murch">
        Walter Murch
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/James_Crutchfield" title="James Crutchfield">
        James Crutchfield
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Christian_de_Duve" title="Christian de Duve">
        Christian de Duve
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Ganson" title="Arthur Ganson">
        Arthur Ganson
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tim_Hunkin" title="Tim Hunkin">
        Tim Hunkin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Hyde" title="Lewis Hyde">
        Lewis Hyde
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Evelyn_Fox_Keller" title="Evelyn Fox Keller">
        Evelyn Fox Keller
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_G%C3%B3mez-Pe%C3%B1a" title="Guillermo Gómez-Peña">
        Guillermo Gómez-Peña
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rosamond_Wolff_Purcell&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rosamond Wolff Purcell (page does not exist)">
        Rosamond Wolff Purcell
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Sacks" title="Oliver Sacks">
        Oliver Sacks
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mierle_Laderman_Ukeles" title="Mierle Laderman Ukeles">
        Mierle Laderman Ukeles
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Felipe_Herrera" title="Juan Felipe Herrera">
        Juan Felipe Herrera
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Osher_79-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Osher-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There are hands-on activities for younger visitors (under 14 - needs confirmation). The pendulum art activity has a youngster picking four different color markers. The youngster then pushes a large board suspended by 4 wires to develop a pattern. At the youngster's say so, the attendant places a selected color into an arm and lowers it onto a white paper weighted to the board. The marker patterns the movement of the board. After 4 markers are done, the project is complete, signed by the 'young artist', and taken home.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Influence">
        Influence
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Exploratorium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Influence">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">
        Impact
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Exploratorium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Impact">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 2007, the Exploratorium was highlighted in the book
       <i>
        Forces For Good
       </i>
       as one of the 12 most effective non-profits in the United States, and was the only West Coast institution and only museum to make the list.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crutchfield_80-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Crutchfield-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It has inspired science museums worldwide, from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reuben_H._Fleet_Science_Center" title="Reuben H. Fleet Science Center">
        Reuben H. Fleet Science Center
       </a>
       in San Diego to the
       <a href="/wiki/Garden_of_Archimedes" title="Garden of Archimedes">
        Garden of Archimedes
       </a>
       in Florence, Italy. In 2003,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Oxford_Companion_to_the_History_of_Modern_Science" title="The Oxford Companion to the History of Modern Science">
         The Oxford Companion to the History of Modern Science
        </a>
       </i>
       noted that about 400 science centers in 43 countries were established after the example of the Exploratorium.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pancaldi_81-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Pancaldi-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Attendance">
        Attendance
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Exploratorium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Attendance">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 2012, 570,000 people visited the Exploratorium; 55% were adults and 45% were children. Geographically, 52% were from the Bay Area, 24% from the rest of California, 14% from other states, and 10% outside the US. Some 36% received free or discounted admission, and 44,000 attended on free admission days. Prior to the relocation, 97,000 students and chaperons visited the museum each year; of these, 67,000 participated in the Field Trip program. It was estimated that 180 million people visited Exploratorium exhibits at science centers and other locations worldwide.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factsheet_57-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-factsheet-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Annual attendance at the new Pier 15 location was anticipated to exceed one million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogers_82-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Rogers-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, in August 2013, the
       <i>
        New York Times
       </i>
       reported that although attendance had soared, revenues still fell short of goals, forcing the Exploratorium to lay off around 1/5 of its staff.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChangCutback_83-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ChangCutback-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Museum officials had decided not to make a big publicity push upon reopening, fearing the overcrowding experienced by the
       <a href="/wiki/California_Academy_of_Sciences" title="California Academy of Sciences">
        California Academy of Sciences
       </a>
       in 2008, but this was later viewed as "an opportunity lost".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChangCutback_83-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ChangCutback-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A staffer (expecting himself to be laid off) observed that the Exploratorium seemed to be "moving from visionary, internally developed work to work-for-hire for other museums around the world”, as the management scrambled to earn more money from consulting for other organizations to replace unrealized admissions revenue.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChangCutback_83-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-ChangCutback-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On April 17, 2014 the Exploratorium announced that attendance in the first year since re-opening was 1.1 million visitors, and that other key statistics had doubled or tripled.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fact2014_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Fact2014-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Website">
        Website
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Exploratorium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Website">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Exploratorium_Webcast.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="429" data-file-width="640" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Exploratorium_Webcast.jpg/300px-Exploratorium_Webcast.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Exploratorium_Webcast.jpg/450px-Exploratorium_Webcast.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Exploratorium_Webcast.jpg/600px-Exploratorium_Webcast.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Exploratorium_Webcast.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Solar Eclipse
         </i>
         webcast at the old Exploratorium.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Online since 1993, the Exploratorium was one of the first museums to build a site on the World Wide Web.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gnatek_84-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Gnatek-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The site serves 13 million visitors each year. It has received six
       <a href="/wiki/Webby_Award" title="Webby Award">
        Webby Awards
       </a>
       since 1997, including four for Best Science Website and one for Best Education website, and has been an honoree an additional ten times.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Webby_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Webby-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Exploratorium's website is an extension of the experiences on the museum's floor and provides a large number of hands-on activities and exhibits for online-only visitors. The Exploratorium also broadcasts live video and/or audio directly from the museum floor (or from satellite feeds in the field, at such locations as Antarctica or the Belize rainforest) onto the Internet from its Webcast Studio. Webcasts provide access to special events, scientists, and other museum resources for audiences on the Web. Visitors to the website can hear or view interviews with scientists, "meet" interesting people, or tour unique locations from factories to particle accelerators.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Semper_86-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Semper-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Exploratorium has additionally released two free iPad apps, Sound Uncovered (2013) and Color Uncovered (2011), which assist in making its unique educational model as accessible as possible. Color Uncovered has been downloaded more than a million times.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iPad_87-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-iPad-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Partnerships">
        Partnerships
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Exploratorium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Partnerships">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Exploratorium has a number of partnerships with other organizations. One notable current partnership is with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Oceanographic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanographic and Atmospheric Administration">
        National Oceanographic and Atmospheric Administration
       </a>
       (NOAA). NOAA research vessels periodically berth at the end of Pier 15 and use the working biological labs featured in the museum to bring their research and data to the public. A number of exhibits at the Exploratorium, such as
       <i>
        Remote Rains
       </i>
       , are based on NOAA data. NOAA scientists additionally provided training for the Explainer program to assist Explainers in explaining science to visitors based on the NOAA’s areas of research.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plutchak_49-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Plutchak-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Global_Studios">
        Global Studios
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Exploratorium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Global Studios">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Exploratorium Global Studios initiative is an entrepreneurial endeavor that shares resources, exhibits, and research with foreign governments, universities, partner museums, libraries, hospitals, and other public and private entities around the world. One area of significant current activity for the Global Studios initiative is the Middle East, where it hopes to assist countries that are making long-term investments in education and transitioning to more information-based economies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GlobalStudios_88-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-GlobalStudios-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For example, the Tinkering Studio visited a science festival in Al Khobar, Saudi Arabia in the summer of 2012, where they trained a group of teachers to help thousands of festival participants to experience the hands-on learning style favored by the Exploratorium.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Visiting_the_museum">
        Visiting the museum
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Exploratorium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Visiting the museum">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wave_Organ_2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Wave_Organ_2.jpg/220px-Wave_Organ_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Wave_Organ_2.jpg/330px-Wave_Organ_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Wave_Organ_2.jpg/440px-Wave_Organ_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wave_Organ_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Wave Organ
         </i>
         is an off-site Exploratorium exhibit
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hours_and_access">
        Hours and access
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Exploratorium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Hours and access">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Exploratorium is open Tuesday through Sunday from 10am-5pm, with adults-only evening hours from 6pm-10pm on Thursdays (for visitors age 18+). The entire museum is wheelchair-accessible.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Exploratorium is located on the
       <a href="/wiki/Embarcadero_(San_Francisco)" title="Embarcadero (San Francisco)">
        Embarcadero
       </a>
       at Green Street, between
       <a href="/wiki/Fisherman%27s_Wharf,_San_Francisco" title="Fisherman's Wharf, San Francisco">
        Fisherman’s Wharf
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Ferry_Building" title="San Francisco Ferry Building">
        Ferry Building
       </a>
       . The museum is accessible by multiple modes of public transit, including
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BART" title="BART">
        BART
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Municipal_Railway" title="San Francisco Municipal Railway">
        Muni
       </a>
       streetcar, bus, taxi, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pedicab" title="Pedicab">
        pedicab
       </a>
       . It is located 0.6 miles (0.97 km) from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embarcadero_Station" title="Embarcadero Station">
        Embarcadero
       </a>
       BART and MUNI stations, and has its own stop on the
       <a href="/wiki/F_Market_%26_Wharves" title="F Market &amp; Wharves">
        F streetcar line
       </a>
       . The Exploratorium does not own or operate any parking lots, but is located near several publicly accessible lots and on-street parking, including a lot directly across the street, operated by the Port of San Francisco.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Related_points_of_interest">
        Related points of interest
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Exploratorium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Related points of interest">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Exploratorium maintains exhibits in public Bay Area spaces. The Outdoor Exploratorium consists of 14 different exhibits relating to the local environment, all placed outside in the
       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Mason" title="Fort Mason">
        Fort Mason
       </a>
       area and accessible to the general public.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FrogMom_90-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FrogMom-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wave_Organ" title="Wave Organ">
         Wave Organ
        </a>
       </i>
       is another notable public artwork of the Exploratorium. Created by former staff artist Peter Richards, this acoustic sculpture is situated on a point of land jutting into the San Francisco Bay not far from the Exploratorium’s original Palace of Fine Arts location.
      </p>
